	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Common raven</h1>
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Raven&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Raven">Northern Raven</a>)</span></div>
		<div id="contentSub2"></div>
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">A large, black, passerine bird of the Northern Hemisphere</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Corvus corax" redirects here. For the German band, see <a href="/wiki/Corvus_Corax_(band)" title="Corvus Corax (band)">Corvus Corax (band)</a>.</div>  
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p><p class="mw-empty-elt">

<td colspan="2" style="text-align: center; font-size: 88%">Common raven range
</td></tr>

<p>The <b>common raven</b> (<i>Corvus corax</i>), also known as the <b>western raven</b> or  <b>northern raven</b> when discussing the raven at the subspecies level, is a large all-black   <a href="/wiki/Passerine" title="Passerine">passerine</a> bird. Found across the Northern Hemisphere, it is the most widely distributed of all <a href="/wiki/Corvidae" title="Corvidae">corvids</a>. There are at least eight <a href="/wiki/Subspecies" title="Subspecies">subspecies</a> with little variation in appearance, although recent research has demonstrated significant genetic differences among populations from various regions. It is one of the two largest corvids, alongside the <a href="/wiki/Thick-billed_raven" title="Thick-billed raven">thick-billed raven</a>, and is possibly the heaviest passerine bird; at maturity, the common raven averages 63 centimetres (25 inches) in length and 1.2 kilograms (2.6 pounds) in mass. Although their typical lifespan is considerably shorter, common ravens can live more than 23 years in the wild,<sup id="cite_ref-euroring_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euroring-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> which among passerines only is surpassed by a few Australian species such as the <a href="/wiki/Satin_bowerbird" title="Satin bowerbird">satin bowerbird</a><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and probably the <a href="/wiki/Lyrebird" title="Lyrebird">lyrebirds</a>. Young birds may travel in flocks but later <a href="/wiki/Mate_for_life" class="mw-redirect" title="Mate for life">mate for life</a>, with each <a href="/wiki/Mated_pair" class="mw-redirect" title="Mated pair">mated pair</a> defending a <a href="/wiki/Territory_(animal)" title="Territory (animal)">territory</a>.
</p><p>Common ravens have coexisted with humans for thousands of years and in some areas have been so numerous that people have regarded them as <a href="/wiki/Pest_(organism)" title="Pest (organism)">pests</a>. Part of their success as a species is due to their <a href="/wiki/Omnivore" title="Omnivore">omnivorous</a> diet: they are extremely versatile and <a href="/wiki/Opportunism#Biological_opportunism" title="Opportunism">opportunistic</a> in finding sources of nutrition, feeding on <a href="/wiki/Carrion" title="Carrion">carrion</a>, insects, cereal grains, berries, fruit, small animals, nesting birds, and food waste.
</p><p>Some notable feats of problem-solving provide evidence that the common raven is unusually <a href="/wiki/Intelligence" title="Intelligence">intelligent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Over the centuries, it has been the subject of mythology, folklore, <a href="/wiki/Cultural_depictions_of_ravens" title="Cultural depictions of ravens">art, and literature</a>. In many cultures, including the indigenous cultures of <a href="/wiki/Norse_mythology" title="Norse mythology">Scandinavia</a>, ancient Ireland and Wales, Bhutan, the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Pacific_Northwest_Coast" title="Indigenous peoples of the Pacific Northwest Coast">northwest coast of North America</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Siberia" title="Indigenous peoples of Siberia">Siberia</a> and northeast Asia, the common raven has been revered as a spiritual figure or godlike creature.<sup id="cite_ref-Jones_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>
<ul>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Taxonomy"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Taxonomy</span></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxonomy">Taxonomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Common_raven&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Taxonomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The common raven was one of the many species originally described by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Linnaeus" title="Carl Linnaeus">Carl Linnaeus</a> in his landmark 1758 <a href="/wiki/10th_edition_of_Systema_Naturae" title="10th edition of Systema Naturae">10th edition of <i>Systema Naturae</i></a>, and it still bears its original name of <i>Corvus corax</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/Type_species" title="Type species">type species</a> of the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Corvus" title="Corvus">Corvus</a></i>, derived from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> word for "raven".<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The specific epithet <i>corax</i> is the Latinized form of the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> word κόραξ meaning "raven" or "crow".<sup id="cite_ref-Liddell1980_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liddell1980-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The modern English word <i>raven</i> has cognates in all other <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic languages</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a> (and subsequently <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">modern Icelandic</a>) <i>hrafn</i><sup id="cite_ref-OED_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OED-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Old_High_German" title="Old High German">Old High German</a> <i>(h)raban</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-OED_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OED-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> all which descend from <a href="/wiki/Proto-Germanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Germanic">Proto-Germanic</a> <i>*khrabanas</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> An old <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scottish</a> word <i>corby</i> or <i>corbie</i>, akin to the French <i>corbeau</i>, has been used for both this bird and the <a href="/wiki/Carrion_crow" title="Carrion crow">carrion crow</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Collective_noun" title="Collective noun">Collective nouns</a> for a group of ravens (or at least the common raven) include "unkindness"<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> and "conspiracy".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Common_raven&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Classification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The closest relatives of the common raven are the <a href="/wiki/Brown-necked_raven" title="Brown-necked raven">brown-necked raven</a> (<i>C. ruficollis</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Pied_crow" title="Pied crow">pied crow</a> (<i>C. albus</i>) of Africa, and the <a href="/wiki/Chihuahuan_raven" title="Chihuahuan raven">Chihuahuan raven</a> (<i>C. cryptoleucus</i>) of the North American Southwest.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> While some authorities have recognized as many as 11 <a href="/wiki/Subspecies" title="Subspecies">subspecies</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-HBW_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HBW-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> others recognize only eight:<sup id="cite_ref-Clements_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clements-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tbody><tr>
<th>Subspecies
</th>
<th>Image
</th>
<th>Distribution
</th>
<th>Notes
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td valign="top"><span class="nowrap"><i>C. c. corax</i></span>, the <b>North Eurasian raven</b>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Corvuscorax001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Corvuscorax001.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Corvuscorax001.jpg/140px-Corvuscorax001.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="94" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Corvuscorax001.jpg/210px-Corvuscorax001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Corvuscorax001.jpg/280px-Corvuscorax001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="438" /></a>
</td>
<td valign="top">From Europe eastwards to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a>, south to the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> region and northern <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>
</td>
<td valign="top">It has a relatively short, arched bill. The population in southwestern Europe (including the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a>) has an even more arched bill and shorter wings than the "typical" nominate, leading some authorities to recognize it as a separate subspecies, the <b>Hispanic raven</b> (<i>C. c. hispanus</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-HBW_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HBW-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td valign="top"><span class="nowrap"><i>C. c. varius</i></span>, the <b>Icelandic raven</b>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Krummi_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Krummi 1.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Krummi_1.jpg/140px-Krummi_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="140" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Krummi_1.jpg/210px-Krummi_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Krummi_1.jpg/280px-Krummi_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="2400" /></a>
</td>
<td valign="top"><a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>
</td>
<td valign="top">It is less glossy than <i>C. c. principalis</i> or the nominate <i>C. c. corax</i>, is intermediate in size, and the bases of its neck feathers are whitish (not visible at a distance). An <a href="/wiki/Extinct" class="mw-redirect" title="Extinct">extinct</a> white-and-black <a href="/wiki/Polymorphism_(biology)" title="Polymorphism (biology)">color morph</a> found only on the Faroes was known as the <b><a href="/wiki/Pied_raven" title="Pied raven">pied raven</a></b> (<i>C. c. varius</i> morpha <i>leucophaeus</i>; the black color morph's scientific name is <i>C. c. varius</i> morpha <i>typicus</i>).
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td valign="top"><span class="nowrap"><i>C. c. subcorax</i></span>, the <b>South Eurasian raven</b>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Corvus_corax_laurencei.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Corvus corax laurencei.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Corvus_corax_laurencei.jpg/140px-Corvus_corax_laurencei.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="95" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Corvus_corax_laurencei.jpg/210px-Corvus_corax_laurencei.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Corvus_corax_laurencei.jpg/280px-Corvus_corax_laurencei.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1389" /></a>
</td>
<td valign="top">From Greece eastwards to northwestern India, Central Asia and western China, though not in the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayan</a> region
</td>
<td valign="top">It is larger than the nominate form, but has relatively short throat feathers (<i>hackles</i>). Its plumage is generally all black, though its neck and breast have a brownish tone similar to that of the brown-necked raven; this is more evident when the plumage is worn. The bases of its neck feathers, although somewhat variable in colour, are often almost whitish.
<p>The name <i>C. c. laurencei</i> (also spelt <i>lawrencii</i> or <i>laurencii</i>) is sometimes used instead of <i>C. c. subcorax</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-HBW_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HBW-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> It is based on the population from <a href="/wiki/Sindh" title="Sindh">Sindh</a> described by <a href="/wiki/Allan_Octavian_Hume" title="Allan Octavian Hume">Hume</a> in 1873<sup id="cite_ref-pcr_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcr-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and is sometimes preferred, since the type specimen of <i>subcorax</i> collected by <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Severtzov" title="Nikolai Severtzov">Nikolai Severtzov</a> is possibly a <a href="/wiki/Brown-necked_raven" title="Brown-necked raven">brown-necked raven</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The population restricted to the <a href="/wiki/Sindh" title="Sindh">Sindh</a> district of Pakistan and adjoining regions of northwestern India is sometimes known as the <b>Punjab raven</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-hbk_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hbk-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td valign="top"><span class="nowrap"><i>C. c. tingitanus</i></span>, the <b>North African raven</b>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:C.corax_tingitanus.JPG" class="image"><img alt="C.corax tingitanus.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/C.corax_tingitanus.JPG/140px-C.corax_tingitanus.JPG" decoding="async" width="140" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/C.corax_tingitanus.JPG/210px-C.corax_tingitanus.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/C.corax_tingitanus.JPG/280px-C.corax_tingitanus.JPG 2x" data-file-width="6016" data-file-height="4000" /></a>
</td>
<td valign="top">North Africa and the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>
</td>
<td valign="top">It is the smallest subspecies, with the shortest throat hackles and a distinctly oily plumage gloss. Its bill is short but markedly stout, and the <a href="/wiki/Culmen_(bird)" class="mw-redirect" title="Culmen (bird)">culmen</a> is strongly arched. The <b>Canary Islands raven</b> is browner than the North African raven, leading some authorities to treat them as separate subspecies with the latter maintaining the name <i>C. c. tingitanus</i> and the former known as <i>C. c. canariensis</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-HBW_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HBW-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td valign="top"><span class="nowrap"><i>C. c. tibetanus</i></span>, the <b>Tibetan raven</b>
</td>
<td valign="top"><a href="/wiki/File:Corvus_corax_tibetanus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Corvus corax tibetanus.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Corvus_corax_tibetanus.jpg/140px-Corvus_corax_tibetanus.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="84" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Corvus_corax_tibetanus.jpg/210px-Corvus_corax_tibetanus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Corvus_corax_tibetanus.jpg/280px-Corvus_corax_tibetanus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2533" data-file-height="1524" /></a>
</td>
<td valign="top">The Himalayas
</td>
<td valign="top">It is the largest and glossiest subspecies, with the longest throat hackles. Its bill is large, but less imposing than that of <i>C. c. principalis</i> and the bases of its neck feathers are grey.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td valign="top"><span class="nowrap"><i>C. c. kamtschaticus</i></span>, the <b>Kamchatkan raven</b>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Corvus_corax_kamtschaticus,_nortern_Mongolia.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Corvus corax kamtschaticus, nortern Mongolia.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Corvus_corax_kamtschaticus%2C_nortern_Mongolia.JPG/140px-Corvus_corax_kamtschaticus%2C_nortern_Mongolia.JPG" decoding="async" width="140" height="105" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Corvus_corax_kamtschaticus%2C_nortern_Mongolia.JPG/210px-Corvus_corax_kamtschaticus%2C_nortern_Mongolia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Corvus_corax_kamtschaticus%2C_nortern_Mongolia.JPG/280px-Corvus_corax_kamtschaticus%2C_nortern_Mongolia.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>
</td>
<td valign="top">Northeastern Asia
</td>
<td valign="top">Intergrades into the nominate subspecies in the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a> region. It is intermediate in size between <i>C. c. principalis</i> and <i>C. c. corax</i> and has a distinctly larger and thicker bill than the nominate subspecies does.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td valign="top"><span class="nowrap"><i>C. c. principalis</i></span>, the <b>northern raven</b>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:3782_Common_Raven_in_flight.jpg" class="image"><img alt="3782 Common Raven in flight.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/3782_Common_Raven_in_flight.jpg/140px-3782_Common_Raven_in_flight.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/3782_Common_Raven_in_flight.jpg/210px-3782_Common_Raven_in_flight.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/3782_Common_Raven_in_flight.jpg/280px-3782_Common_Raven_in_flight.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2157" data-file-height="1434" /></a>
</td>
<td valign="top">Northern North America and <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>
</td>
<td valign="top">It has a large body and the largest bill, its plumage is strongly glossed, and its throat hackles are well developed.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td valign="top"><span class="nowrap"><i>C. c. sinuatus</i></span>, the <b>western raven</b>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Corvus_corax_clarionensis_perched_frontal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Corvus corax clarionensis perched frontal.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Corvus_corax_clarionensis_perched_frontal.jpg/140px-Corvus_corax_clarionensis_perched_frontal.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="210" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Corvus_corax_clarionensis_perched_frontal.jpg/210px-Corvus_corax_clarionensis_perched_frontal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Corvus_corax_clarionensis_perched_frontal.jpg/280px-Corvus_corax_clarionensis_perched_frontal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="533" data-file-height="800" /></a>
</td>
<td valign="top">South-central North America and Central America
</td>
<td valign="top">It is smaller, with a smaller and narrower bill than <i>C. c. principalis</i>. Populations in the far southwestern U.S. and northwestern Mexico (including the <a href="/wiki/Revillagigedo_Islands" title="Revillagigedo Islands">Revillagigedo Islands</a>) are the smallest in North America. They are sometimes included in <i>C. c. sinuatus</i>, while other authorities recognize them as a distinct subspecies, the <b>southwestern raven</b> (<i>C. c. clarionensis</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-HBW_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HBW-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evolutionary_history">Evolutionary history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Common_raven&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Evolutionary history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The common raven evolved in the <a href="/wiki/Old_World" title="Old World">Old World</a> and crossed the <a href="/wiki/Bering_land_bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Bering land bridge">Bering land bridge</a> into North America.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Recent genetic studies, which examined the <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> of common ravens from across the world, have determined that the birds fall into at least two <a href="/wiki/Clade" title="Clade">clades</a>: a <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> clade, found only in the southwestern United States, and a <a href="/wiki/Holarctic" class="mw-redirect" title="Holarctic">Holarctic</a> clade, found across the rest of the Northern Hemisphere. Birds from both clades look alike, but the groups are genetically distinct and began to diverge about two million years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The findings indicate that based on <a href="/wiki/Mitochondrial_DNA" title="Mitochondrial DNA">mitochondrial DNA</a>, common ravens from the rest of the United States are more closely related to those in Europe and Asia than to those in the California clade, and that common ravens in the California clade are more closely related to the <a href="/wiki/Chihuahuan_raven" title="Chihuahuan raven">Chihuahuan raven</a> (<i>C. cryptoleucus</i>) than to those in the Holarctic clade.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Ravens in the Holarctic clade are more closely related to the <a href="/wiki/Pied_crow" title="Pied crow">pied crow</a> (<i>C. albus</i>) than they are to the California clade.<sup id="cite_ref-Feld05_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feld05-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Thus, the common raven species as traditionally delimited is considered to be <a href="/wiki/Paraphyletic" class="mw-redirect" title="Paraphyletic">paraphyletic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Feld05_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feld05-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>One explanation for these genetic findings is that common ravens settled in California at least two million years ago and became separated from their relatives in Europe and Asia during an <a href="/wiki/Ice_age" title="Ice age">ice age</a>. One million years ago, a group from the California clade evolved into a new species, the Chihuahuan raven. Other members of the Holarctic clade arrived later in a separate migration from Asia, perhaps at the same time as humans.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2011 study suggested that there are no restrictions on <a href="/wiki/Gene_flow" title="Gene flow">gene flow</a> between the Californian and Holarctic common raven groups, and that the lineages can remerge, effectively reversing a potential speciation.<sup id="cite_ref-random_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-random-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A recent study of raven mitochondrial DNA showed that the isolated population from the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> is distinct from other populations.<sup id="cite_ref-Bakom06_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bakom06-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The study did not include any individuals from the North African population,<sup id="cite_ref-Bakom06_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bakom06-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and its position is therefore unclear, though its <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(biology)" title="Morphology (biology)">morphology</a> is very close to the population of the Canaries (to the extent that the two are often considered part of a single subspecies).<sup id="cite_ref-Clements_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clements-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Description">Description</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Common_raven&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Description">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For physiology, see <a href="/wiki/Common_raven_physiology" title="Common raven physiology">Common raven physiology</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Raven_Cypress_Provincial_Park_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Raven_Cypress_Provincial_Park_2.JPG/220px-Raven_Cypress_Provincial_Park_2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Raven_Cypress_Provincial_Park_2.JPG/330px-Raven_Cypress_Provincial_Park_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Raven_Cypress_Provincial_Park_2.JPG/440px-Raven_Cypress_Provincial_Park_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1349" data-file-height="985" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Raven_Cypress_Provincial_Park_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In sunlight, the <a href="/wiki/Plumage" title="Plumage">plumage</a> can display a blue or purple sheen which is a result of <a href="/wiki/Iridescence" title="Iridescence">iridescence</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>A mature common raven ranges between 54 and 67&#160;cm (21" and 26") long, with a <a href="/wiki/Wingspan" title="Wingspan">wingspan</a> of 115 to 150&#160;cm (45–51").<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Recorded weights range from 0.69 to 2&#160;kg (1.5 to 4.4&#160;lb),<sup id="cite_ref-Boarman_Heinrich_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boarman_Heinrich-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> thus making the common raven one of the heaviest <a href="/wiki/Passerine" title="Passerine">passerines</a>. Birds from colder regions such as the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a> and Greenland are generally larger with slightly larger bills, while those from warmer regions are smaller with proportionally smaller bills.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Representative of the size variation in the species, ravens from <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> weighed an average of 784&#160;g (1.728&#160;lb), those from <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> weighed an average of 1,135&#160;g (2.502&#160;lb) and those from <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> weighed an average of 1,230&#160;g (2.71&#160;lb).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Beak" title="Beak">bill</a> is large and slightly curved, with a <a href="/wiki/Culmen_(bird)" class="mw-redirect" title="Culmen (bird)">culmen</a> length of 5.7 to 8.5&#160;cm (2.2 to 3.3&#160;in), easily one of the largest bills amongst passerines (perhaps only the <a href="/wiki/Thick-billed_raven" title="Thick-billed raven">thick-billed raven</a> has a noticeably larger bill). It has a longish, strongly graduated tail, at 20 to 26.3&#160;cm (7.9 to 10.4&#160;in), and mostly black <a href="/wiki/Iridescent" class="mw-redirect" title="Iridescent">iridescent</a> plumage, and a dark brown <a href="/wiki/Iris_(anatomy)" title="Iris (anatomy)">iris</a>. The throat feathers are elongated and pointed and the bases of the neck feathers are pale brownish-grey. The legs and feet are good-sized, with a <a href="/wiki/Tarsus_(skeleton)" title="Tarsus (skeleton)">tarsus</a> length of 6 to 7.2&#160;cm (2.4 to 2.8&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Juvenile plumage is similar but duller with a blue-grey iris.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Apart from its greater size, the common raven differs from its cousins, the <a href="/wiki/Crow" title="Crow">crows</a>, by having a larger and heavier black beak, shaggy feathers around the throat and above the beak, and a wedge-shaped tail.<sup id="cite_ref-observerbook_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-observerbook-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Flying ravens are distinguished from crows by their tail shape, larger wing area, and more stable soaring style, which generally involves less wing flapping. Despite their bulk, ravens are easily as agile in flight as their smaller cousins. In flight the feathers produce a creaking sound that has been likened to the rustle of silk.<sup id="cite_ref-hbk_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hbk-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The voice of ravens is also quite distinct, its usual call being a deep croak of a much more sonorous quality than a crow's call. In North America, the <a href="/wiki/Chihuahuan_raven" title="Chihuahuan raven">Chihuahuan raven</a> (<i>C. cryptoleucus</i>) is fairly similar to the relatively small common ravens of the American southwest and is best distinguished by the still relatively smaller size of its bill, beard and body and relatively longer tail. All-black <a href="/wiki/Carrion_crow" title="Carrion crow">carrion crow</a> (<i>C. corone</i>) in Europe may suggest a raven due to their largish bill but are still distinctly smaller and have the wing and tail shapes typical of crows.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>, a now-extinct white-and-black colour morph of this species existed, known as the <a href="/wiki/Pied_raven" title="Pied raven">pied raven</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>White ravens are occasionally found in the wild. Birds in <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> lack the pink eyes of an albino, and are instead <a href="/wiki/Leucistic" class="mw-redirect" title="Leucistic">leucistic</a>, a condition where an animal lacks any of several different types of pigment, not simply <a href="/wiki/Melanin" title="Melanin">melanin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dearing_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dearing-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
